  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c840f74d-cbde-435d-99fc-8596ea2aabc8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer6738104036607018542">A magical island. A dangerous task. A burning secret.<br/><br/>Linus Baker leads a quiet, solitary life. At forty, he lives in a tiny house with a devious cat and his old records.   <span id="freeText6738104036607018542" style="display:none">A magical island. A dangerous task. A burning secret.<br /><br />Linus Baker leads a quiet, solitary life. At forty, he lives in a tiny house with a devious cat and his old records. As a Case Worker at the Department in Charge Of Magical Youth, he spends his days overseeing the well-being of children in government-sanctioned orphanages.<br /><br />When Linus is unexpectedly summoned by Extremely Upper Management he's given a curious and highly classified assignment: travel to Marsyas Island Orphanage, where six dangerous children reside: a gnome, a sprite, a wyvern, an unidentifiable green blob, a were-Pomeranian, and the Antichrist. Linus must set aside his fears and determine whether or not they’re likely to bring about the end of days.<br /><br />But the children aren’t the only secret the island keeps. Their caretaker is the charming and enigmatic Arthur Parnassus, who will do anything to keep his wards safe. As Arthur and Linus grow closer, long-held secrets are exposed, and Linus must make a choice: destroy a home or watch the world burn.<br /><br />An enchanting story, masterfully told, <i>The House in the Cerulean Sea</i> is about the profound experience of discovering an unlikely family in an unexpected place—and realizing that family is yours.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6738104036607018542" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/66357746-david"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1490671908i/66357746.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/66357746-david">David</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I would really say that it depends on the 9 year old. I read "Carrie" when I was 9. My mother knew that I could handle it. The parts that I didn't und<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I would really say that it depends on the 9 year old. I read "Carrie" when I was 9. My mother knew that I could handle it. The parts that I didn't understand caused me to ask questions. <br /><br />There is a blossuming gay relationship in this book. If your 9 year old is aware of such things, then the book is fine. If he's not, it might be an opportunity to teach. But the relationship is described with a great deal of care, and there is nothing sexual depicted. I'm sure some children would read it as the two simply being close friends.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_3103716929" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3103716929" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3103716929?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=2020-releases">2020-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-slow-burn">trope-slow-burn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult-romance">adult-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-grumpy-mc-sunshine-mc">trope-grumpy-mc-sunshine-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-idiots-in-love">trope-idiots-in-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-rep">lgbtq-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-mm">lgbtq-mm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-rivals-to-lovers">trope-rivals-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-found-family">trope-found-family</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3103716929" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17448359153140608483">✧ <a href='https://bookswithchaima.wordpress.com/2020/04/20/review-the-house-in-the-cerulean-sea-by-t-j-klune/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <b>find this review & others on my blog</b>
</a> ✧<br/><br/>I think these days more than ever, with a pandemic ravaging every corner of the world, I understand more keenly how absolutely necessary it is to find the escape hatch in reality, to seek out a pleasant corner and while away the hours inside a story. And there is no better one I can think of than this one.<br/><br/><strong>“<em>The House in the Cerulean Sea</em>” is a nonstop pleasure.</strong> It flooded every corner of my mind with delight and warmth and made me feel reassured and nour</span>
  <span id="freeText17448359153140608483" style="display:none">✧ <a href="https://bookswithchaima.wordpress.com/2020/04/20/review-the-house-in-the-cerulean-sea-by-t-j-klune/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>find this review &amp; others on my blog</b>
</a> ✧<br /><br />I think these days more than ever, with a pandemic ravaging every corner of the world, I understand more keenly how absolutely necessary it is to find the escape hatch in reality, to seek out a pleasant corner and while away the hours inside a story. And there is no better one I can think of than this one.<br /><br /><strong>“<em>The House in the Cerulean Sea</em>” is a nonstop pleasure.</strong> It flooded every corner of my mind with delight and warmth and made me feel reassured and nourished in channels of my heart which had stood scraped dry for weeks. It’s a feeling I wish I could put in a bottle to carry it with me through the dark.<br /><br />The novel's premise is as simple as it is ripe with comic potential. Caseworker Linus Baker of the Department in Charge of Magical Youths (DICOMY) has the distinct appearance of someone with a stick up his ass. His job is like a millstone, all weight and no warmth: investigate orphanages that house magical children, write a report that encourages either the continuation or discontinuation of these establishments, and justify it all within the uncompromising parameters of <em>fairness</em>. See, Linus Baker follows the rules with an unflinching rigidity, walking through life like a wound-up clock ticking dutifully through the seconds. But when Linus is assigned to investigate an island orphanage for magical children deemed especially dangerous, his world is like a house with all its doors thrown wide open, so many new rooms added to a place he was so sure he already knew.<br /><br />There is something vital and wondrous about Arthur and the magical children that came to him with tragedies already packed in their suitcases, and Linus Baker is more or less the human opposite of vitality and wonder. During his stay in the house in the Cerulean sea, Linus becomes acutely, achingly aware of the empty place at his center, and starts wondering at the grim march of the life he’d lived before. A life that once seemed perfectly fine, but which now pinches like tight shoes.<br /><br />TJ Klune wears his heart on his sleeve, and “<em>The House in the Cerulean Sea</em>” is that much better for it. The novel is lively, exquisitely crafted and wildly propulsive. It brims and bubbles with quirkiness and playful detail, and the dialogue positively fizzes.<br /><br /><strong>But it’s the cast of tenderly realized characters that carries the day.</strong><br /><br />There is something undeniably unconditional about the relationships here, and it stirred my heart. Klune’s cast of characters is achingly compelling. Arthur’s lightness of heart is infectious; he is a study in kindness, made of such a steadfast and dependable fiber. His magical children are every inch as erratic and colorful as Linus is restrained and monochromatic, and together they made something like the word “family”, disappearing into one another like partly shuffled cards, and rubbing their rough edges smooth against each other. I can’t tell you how much I relish stories that don’t believe that blood makes a family, but that kin is the circle you create, hands held tight. Linus, Arthur and the kids could not have been more different, but they all formed the same desperate plea in their minds: to be seen, to be loved, to reach and to be reached for. And as they all moved, tremulously, one step along the road between unknown and familiar, I found myself full of wishes for them—for that house in the Cerulean sea, away from the gaze of malice and a happily-ever-after.<br /><br />But as entertaining and unrelentingly fun “<em>The House in the Cerulean Sea</em>” is, it is hard to forget that it’s also calmly, intelligently damning, and full of tough questions about difference, prejudice and complacency. The novel delicately carves out the myriad ways in which we see and don’t see our own world and the people around us. It questions our tendency to categorize things to make them easier to understand, to slip into stereotypes that create more fear than the reality. That said, “The House in the Cerulean Sea” is leavened with hope. It knows hate, but believes in people too. It’s a celebration of the nondiscriminatory nature of love that thoughtfully explores not only its rewards but its risks too.<br /><br />All in all, “The House in the Cerulean Sea” is a cracking, charming novel, and I find myself hoping for a sequel. In fact, knowing this is a standalone, and there are no more books to come in this wonderful world is the novel’s only disappointment.<br /><br /><blockquote>☆ <a href="https://ko-fi.com/givemeabrekk" rel="nofollow noopener">ko-fi</a> ★ <a href="https://bookswithchaima.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> ☆ <a href="https://twitter.com/proyearner" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> ★ <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">tumblr</a> ☆</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="17448359153140608483" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2734393033" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2734393033" />
    <a title="Heather K (dentist in my spare time)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time"><img alt="Heather K (dentist in my spare time)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365526640p2/13070326.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2734393033?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather K (dentist in my spare time)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather K (dentist in my spare time)" href="/user/show/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time">Heather K (dentist in my spare time)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781250217288" href="/book/show/45046567-the-house-in-the-cerulean-sea">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=read-to-review-arc">read-to-review-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=fae">fae</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=loved-it">loved-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=m-m">m-m</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=little-to-no-sex-content">little-to-no-sex-content</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=lgbtq-lit">lgbtq-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=favorites-2020">favorites-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2734393033" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1207595695027674039"><b>An extraordinary treat for both <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5073330.T_J__Klune' title='T.J. Klune' rel='nofollow noopener'>T.J. Klune</a> fans and those new to his writing, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45047384.The_House_in_the_Cerulean_Sea' title='The House in the Cerulean Sea by T.J. Klune' rel='nofollow noopener'>The House in the Cerulean Sea</a> is a heart-warming, wholesome, diverse, ridiculous, and completely lovable fantasy story.</b> <br/><br/>As a long-time <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5073330.T_J__Klune' title='T.J. Klune' rel='nofollow noopener'>T.J. Klune</a> fan, as I'm sure many of you are, I know you are asking yourself what this book will be like now that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5073330.T_J__Klune' title='T.J. Klune' rel='nofollow noopener'>T.J. Klune</a> is publishing with the big boys. I'm very happy to report that the book read just like I was expecting it to, which means <b>tight writing, <i>romance</i> (!), queer charact</b></span>
  <span id="freeText1207595695027674039" style="display:none"><b>An extraordinary treat for both <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5073330.T_J__Klune" title="T.J. Klune" rel="nofollow noopener">T.J. Klune</a> fans and those new to his writing, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45047384.The_House_in_the_Cerulean_Sea" title="The House in the Cerulean Sea by T.J. Klune" rel="nofollow noopener">The House in the Cerulean Sea</a> is a heart-warming, wholesome, diverse, ridiculous, and completely lovable fantasy story.</b> <br /><br />As a long-time <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5073330.T_J__Klune" title="T.J. Klune" rel="nofollow noopener">T.J. Klune</a> fan, as I'm sure many of you are, I know you are asking yourself what this book will be like now that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5073330.T_J__Klune" title="T.J. Klune" rel="nofollow noopener">T.J. Klune</a> is publishing with the big boys. I'm very happy to report that the book read just like I was expecting it to, which means <b>tight writing, <i>romance</i> (!), queer characters everywhere (<i>natch</i>), and a story you won't want to put down.</b><br /><br />I wasn't sure how this book would be, to be honest, because it is billed as "contemporary fantasy," and I'm not really a <i>fantasy</i> reader. And, really, I'm surprised it's a contemporary because I would have placed the timeline as further in the past due to some of the details, but that's not really here nor there. It isn't an high fantasy, so it is good for low fantasy readers who simply like a little magic in their world, like me. But the bottom line is <b>if you've enjoyed TJ's books in the past, you'll love this story. And if you are new to him, you'll soon be devouring his backlist. Welcome to the club.</b><br /><br />I think this book could be enjoyed by all readers of all ages. It is probably meant for adults, but it's a great read for those as young as middle grade (I would let my 5th grader read it if her reading level was advanced enough). It has a lot of important lessons about how we judge one another and what our preconceived notions are about other people, and in this world, the more gentle learning we can take in, the better. It does edge a bit towards sentimental at times, but it just adds to the charm. <br /><br /><b>TJ is very adept at writing interesting young characters, and that's where this book really shines.</b> The children in this story are all heart-breaking, and <i>funny</i> (the BEST parts of the story), and you'll fall in love with them all. I would be hard-pressed to pick my favorites, but Lucy and Chauncey stood out for me. Lucy has some of the best contrasts in the book, and Chauncey is just so <i>pure</i>. <i>*1,000 heart-eye emojis.*</i><br /><br />The story is fairly long, but that just means more to savor. You won't be bored for one minute, and you'll leave the story feeling happy and hopeful. <br /><br /><b>With his typical beautiful writing and unique style, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5073330.T_J__Klune" title="T.J. Klune" rel="nofollow noopener">T.J. Klune</a> makes <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45047384.The_House_in_the_Cerulean_Sea" title="The House in the Cerulean Sea by T.J. Klune" rel="nofollow noopener">The House in the Cerulean Sea</a> shine.</b> With no end to his imagination in sight, I can't wait to see what TJ will come up with next. <br /><br /><br />*Copy provided in exchange for an honest review*<br /><br /> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time" rel="nofollow noopener">goodreads</a>|<a href="https://www.instagram.com/heatherk_dentistinmysparetime/" rel="nofollow noopener">instagram</a>|<a href="https://twitter.com/DentistHeatherK" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a>|<a href="http://www.myfictionnook.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1207595695027674039" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3291787438" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3291787438" />
    <a title="Chelsea (chelseadolling reads)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16219087-chelsea-chelseadolling-reads"><img alt="Chelsea (chelseadolling reads)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566850655p2/16219087.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3291787438?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea (chelseadolling reads)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea (chelseadolling reads)" href="/user/show/16219087-chelsea-chelseadolling-reads">Chelsea (chelseadolling reads)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<div id="review_3322389669" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3322389669" />
    <a title="Melissa ~ Bantering Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33853154-melissa-bantering-books"><img alt="Melissa ~ Bantering Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584398324p2/33853154.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3322389669?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ~ Bantering Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ~ Bantering Books" href="/user/show/33853154-melissa-bantering-books">Melissa ~ Bantering Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781250217288" href="/book/show/45046567-the-house-in-the-cerulean-sea">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33853154-melissa-bantering-books?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3322389669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3983519530471231630"><b>
  <i> “His thoughts were all cerulean.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>Mine, too. My thoughts are all cerulean, now that I have read TJ Klune’s wonderful novel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45047384.The_House_in_the_Cerulean_Sea' title='The House in the Cerulean Sea by T.J. Klune' rel='nofollow noopener'>The House in the Cerulean Sea</a>. And never have they been tinted such a brilliant, exquisite shade of blue. <br/><br/>Linus Baker lives routinely by the rules. He is a dedicated caseworker for the Department in Charge of Magical Youth; he knows every word of its <i>RULES AND REGULATIONS</i> by heart. At the end of each workday, he returns home to an empty house, comforted only by his clas</span>
  <span id="freeText3983519530471231630" style="display:none"><b>
  <i> “His thoughts were all cerulean.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Mine, too. My thoughts are all cerulean, now that I have read TJ Klune’s wonderful novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/45047384.The_House_in_the_Cerulean_Sea" title="The House in the Cerulean Sea by T.J. Klune" rel="nofollow noopener">The House in the Cerulean Sea</a>. And never have they been tinted such a brilliant, exquisite shade of blue. <br /><br />Linus Baker lives routinely by the rules. He is a dedicated caseworker for the Department in Charge of Magical Youth; he knows every word of its <i>RULES AND REGULATIONS</i> by heart. At the end of each workday, he returns home to an empty house, comforted only by his classic record collection and his cantankerous (but lovable) cat, Calliope.<br /><br />Then unexpectedly, Linus is given a top-secret assignment by Extremely Upper Management. His mission? To travel to a clandestine orphanage on Marsyas Island, where six highly magical, highly dangerous children live. While there, Linus is expected to observe both the children and the master of the orphanage, Arthur Parnassus, report his findings to Extremely Upper Management, and ultimately determine whether the orphanage should be closed.<br /><br />But as in all good tales, Linus soon finds there is much more to Arthur and the children than meets the eye. And much to his astonishment, he also discovers a quiet yearning within his own heart for a life he never even knew he wanted.<br /><br />Prepare yourselves. I am about to gush. Profusely.<br /><br /><i>The House in the Cerulean Sea</i> is an absolute treasure. It is a pot of gold found at the end of a rainbow. It is a priceless jewel cupped protectively in one’s hands. It is a perfectly delicious sundae with a cherry on top. It is a golden ray of sunlight shining through the blackest of clouds. It is a stunningly spectacular summer sunset.<br /><br />And bar none, it is the kindest, gentlest, most loving story I have ever read. <i>Ever</i>. Love and kindness virtually radiate from Klune’s words and ever so tenderly spiral around you like a soft, warm blanket. The entire reading experience is incredibly comforting and calming.<br /><br />Like Linus, the novel is one that I never even knew I needed. Or wanted. I am grateful to have found it.<br /><br />Klune’s tale is, for sure, a fantastical one, filled with lovable magical children and endearing magical creatures. It has charm, whimsy, and a touch of romance. It has gorgeously simple writing. <br /><br />It also has impeccable humor. The novel is truly hysterical, in a cleverly dry and witty sort of way. It may very well be the most amusing story I have ever read.<br /><br />But do you know what I love most about <i>The House in the Cerulean Sea</i>? <br /><br />Its gently powerful messages. Because not only is the novel about kindness – it’s about prejudice and how its roots burrow in fear and misunderstanding. It’s about encouraging people to be who they are and accepting and loving them for it. It’s about the freedom to love whomever you want to love, wholly and freely.<br /><br />It’s beautiful. Klune has written a beautiful, beautiful book.<br /><br />Indeed, the story does feel slightly preachy and a bit syrupy at times. The narrative is also quite predictable and crammed with many common literary tropes. But really, none of it matters. <br /><br />Why? Because the <i>The House in the Cerulean Sea</i> is <i>special</i>. Books as unforgettable as this are few and far between. And even though it may feel like you’ve previously read this story, there is an exceptionally good chance you will adore it more than all the others that have come before.<br /><br />Sincerely, I cannot recommend this novel highly enough. I will never be able to gather the proper words to accurately express how I marvel at the magic of this story.<br /><br />I know, deep within my soul, that it should not be missed by anyone, as it is so lovingly written <i>for</i> everyone. <br /><br />Anyone and everyone with a beating heart, that is. <br /><br />And if, regrettably, you have misplaced your heart somewhere on this treacherous road known as life. . . <i>The House in the Cerulean Sea</i> may be just the story you need to find it once again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3983519530471231630" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3236930039" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17855239975132485614"><br/><b>This little gem totally snuck up on me, but I totally fell in love with both the story and every single one of the characters -- especially the six supernatural kids.<br/><br/><a href='https://imgur.com/VxAUoxL' rel='nofollow noopener'><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1590871173ra/29568073.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/></a><br/><br/>For the first ten percent (ish) of the book, we were introduced to Linus, who led a boring existence, simply going thru the motions, with no real life or friends to speak of.<br/><br/>These parts had a teeny tiny bit of humor, but honestly, if I hadn't already known that Klune wrote it, there wasn't anything to really indicate that fact for m</b></span>
  <span id="freeText17855239975132485614" style="display:none"><br><b>This little gem totally snuck up on me, but I totally fell in love with both the story and every single one of the characters -- especially the six supernatural kids.<br><br><a href="https://imgur.com/VxAUoxL" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1590871173ra/29568073.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>For the first ten percent (ish) of the book, we were introduced to Linus, who led a boring existence, simply going thru the motions, with no real life or friends to speak of.<br><br>These parts had a teeny tiny bit of humor, but honestly, if I hadn't already known that Klune wrote it, there wasn't anything to really indicate that fact for me. Mainly because I was kind of... bored?<br><br>The cure for that boredom was administered and immediately took effect the moment that Linus stepped off the train on his way to the island.<br><br>As a case worker for the Department in Charge of Magical Youth (DICOMY), Linus' initial reception by the residents of the island couldn't be called a warm one, but then again, their fates were all tied to his investigation, so you couldn't exactly blame them.<br><br>As the story proceeded, and the fact that Linus genuinely cared for both their mental and physical well-being, one by one, everyone on the island not only came to trust him, but also genuinely care for him in return.<br><br>And Linus' previously boring and predictable life changed very much for the better, which was damned awesome to witness.<br><br>This was truly a book best approached knowing very little about the island's inhabitants ahead of time, so I'll just say that they were a pleasant mixture of shy, devious, morbid, inquisitive, adventurous, and funny, which really worked well in pulling the reader in and getting them completely invested.<br><br>The drama in the story was divided between the threat of Linus' investigation allowing the DICOMY to close down the orphanage and the backwards views (and threats) from some of the townsfolk in the village close to the island, but both resulted in manageable levels of angst.<br><br>The level of feels in the story was relatively high, with both the "<i>record money</i>" and "<i>buttons</i>" parts seriously pulling at my heart strings. I never cried, but it was a close thing a couple of times, let me tell you.<br><br>Aside from the humor, my favorite parts of the book were when both of the MC's became fiercely protective of the children, going to any lengths required to ensure their safety and happiness.<br><br>If Klune's usual readers find any fault with this story, I strongly suspect it would be in regard to the love story.<br><br>Was there a romance? Yes. But is this <i>predominantly</i> a romance? No, not a very in-depth one, even if the story didn't demand one to feel complete.<br><br>Overall, I'd rate this book at around 4.75 "<i>Don’t you wish you were here?</i>" stars and strongly recommend it to both fans of TJ and also readers looking for something slightly different.<br><br>-----------------------------------------------<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/list/12415682-todd?order=d&amp;sort=date_read&amp;view=reviews" rel="nofollow noopener">See All My Latest Reads (Review Quick-Links)</a><br><br>-----------------------------------------------</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="17855239975132485614" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3437763636" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3437763636" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3437763636?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781250217288" href="/book/show/45046567-the-house-in-the-cerulean-sea">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3437763636" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3092321459742687173">This is a birthday cake of a book. Perhaps a birthday cake dressed up in scary themes, but ultimately, a heart-warming, delicious concoction of a story that <i>just</i> skirts being teeth-tinglingly sweet.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1594657143i/29808473._SX540_.jpg' width='360' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Thankfully, the children in the story are monsters enough to cut the sugar with a little milk.<br/><br/>I enjoyed <i>Cerulean Sea,</i> especially once our milquetoast hero, Linus, makes his way to the orphanage and meets the <i>very special</i> children The Department In Charge of Magical Youth wants examined. Until then, t</span>
  <span id="freeText3092321459742687173" style="display:none">This is a birthday cake of a book. Perhaps a birthday cake dressed up in scary themes, but ultimately, a heart-warming, delicious concoction of a story that <i>just</i> skirts being teeth-tinglingly sweet.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1594657143i/29808473._SX540_.jpg" width="360" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Thankfully, the children in the story are monsters enough to cut the sugar with a little milk.<br><br>I enjoyed <i>Cerulean Sea,</i> especially once our milquetoast hero, Linus, makes his way to the orphanage and meets the <i>very special</i> children The Department In Charge of Magical Youth wants examined. Until then, the build is slow going, as Linus lives in the black and white version of the world. It reminded me, perhaps unsurprisingly, of all the horrible conformity scenes in all the children's books I've ever read, particularly Doris Umbridge shouting over Potter, and those creepy synchronized children in the land controlled by It in <i>A Wrinkle in Time.</i> So: boring, creepy, overt. Let's get to Oz, shall we?<br><br><b><br>"Lucy puffed out his chest. 'I'm brave! And since I'm the leader, my brave order will be that Arthur goes first to make sure it's safe while the rest of us wait right here.'<br>Everyone nodded.<br>Including Linus.<br>Arthur arched an eyebrow at him.<br>'He has a point,' Linus said. 'Bravery is a virtue and all that.'<br>'Arthur's lips twitched. 'If I must.'<br>'You must,' Lucy told him. 'And if there are cannibals, yell back at us when they start to eat you so we know to run away.'<br>'What if they eat my mouth first?'"</b><br><br>Oz is where the magic happens, and where Linus suddenly connects with people, or at least, the children who live in the isolated orphanage. There's Chauncey, the nightmare who dreams of being a bellhop; Talia, the bearded gnome; Phee the forest sprite; Theodore the wyvern; Sid, who has a contagious form of the were virus; and Lucy. Talia has an obsession with graveyards and would love the opportunity to bury someone. When she first meets Linus, she rather hopes he would be her first.<br><b><br>“'You've gone awfully pale,' Talia said as she squinted up at him. 'And you're swaying. Are you ill? If you are, I think we should go back to the garden so you can die there. I don't want to have to drag you all the way back. You look really heavy.' She reached up and poked his stomach. 'So soft.'<br>I’m not ill,” he snapped at her. “I’m just processing.” <br>“Oh. That’s too bad. If your left upper arm starts to hurt, would you let me know?” <br>“Why would I – that’s a sign of a heart attack, isn’t it?”<br></b><br>So, of course Linus' heart grows three sizes, and he has to learn to stop being such a rule-follower and start actually standing up for a principle. All's well and good, isn't it?<br><br>Well, mostly. There's a few problems. Linus' internal voice is mostly observational, spending most of it's time observing his own feelings at that, and not particularly introspective or analytical. From the first scene, this is pointed out to him by a witch at an orphanage he's assessing, and while it presumably hits home, he doesn't analyze it much. So the reader has to <i>interpret</i> Linus' journey. Did he make it out of personal growth? Were the children a catalyst? Was it happening anyway? Or was this about L-U-V? There is telling, and there is showing, but there is also <i>processing</i> and how did we get there? Because it's one thing to have a Grinch have his heart grow three sizes; it's quite another to take a forty-year-old and make them willing to upend their life (and their career of seventeen years). I'm not saying I don't <i>believe,</i> because, honestly, who wouldn't want to hang out with a button-hunting wyvern and create awesome gardens with a gnome? but well, maybe I kinda am. Because I want to know how it's done.<br><br>But yes, those are the grown-up details that only occur after you finish reading it, or when you have to go back to real life and pay the insurance bill or something like that. The story itself is eminently charming and while it is very clear with its message of tolerance, it's a message that really deserves to be heard. And apparently some people do deserve hitting over the head. And if a garden gnome wants to take them and bury them in the garden, who am I to complain? At least fertilizer is useful.<br><br>So, read if you like birthday cake--the good kind, not the sickly sweet, teeth-itching kind--and want a change from the dark and dismal.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3092321459742687173" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3535778523" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3535778523" />
    <a title="Danielle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23302801-danielle"><img alt="Danielle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591067005p2/23302801.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3535778523?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danielle" href="/user/show/23302801-danielle">Danielle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3535778523" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11302427180660379914">This was a magical adventure! 🙌 In my mind: it’s The Ministry of Magic checking in on Miss Peregrine's Home for Peculiar Children. Linus was a great character. He is essentially a CPS officer tasked with checking in on magical orphanages. 🤓 I loved how he interacted with each kid, even though he tried to keep a guard up. Lucy (aka Lucifer) was hilariously candid. 😈 Oh, and Arthur is a Dumbledore/Miss Peregrine for sure! Some of the story felt a bit lagging, but overall it was a great read. 👍</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3464994812" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3464994812" />
    <a title="Hamad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad"><img alt="Hamad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577880699p2/54464244.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3464994812?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hamad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hamad" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad">Hamad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=adult-books">adult-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=book-club">book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=good-covers">good-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=tear-worthy-books">tear-worthy-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3464994812" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10432814259735545629"><a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2020/10/31/the-house-in-the-cerulean-sea-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>This Review</a> ✍️ <a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blog</a> 📖 <a href='https://twitter.com/Hamad9626' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> 🐦 <a href='https://www.instagram.com/thebookprescription/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> 📷<br/> <br/> <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “We should always make time for the things we like. If we don’t, we might forget how to be happy.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>This book has been getting all kind of glowing reviews and I am jumping on the bandwagon and adding my voice to all the fans of this story. This is a book that just made me happy and made me cry and for that it deserves a full 5 stars which I rarely give.<br/><br/>I have not read Klune’s other books and although this is his latest, it was my first expo</span>
  <span id="freeText10432814259735545629" style="display:none"><a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2020/10/31/the-house-in-the-cerulean-sea-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">This Review</a> ✍️ <a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> 📖 <a href="https://twitter.com/Hamad9626" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> 🐦 <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookprescription/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> 📷<br /> <br /> <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “We should always make time for the things we like. If we don’t, we might forget how to be happy.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />This book has been getting all kind of glowing reviews and I am jumping on the bandwagon and adding my voice to all the fans of this story. This is a book that just made me happy and made me cry and for that it deserves a full 5 stars which I rarely give.<br /><br />I have not read Klune’s other books and although this is his latest, it was my first exposure to his works and I have a feeling he would become a favorite author of mine as I make my way through the rest of his books. The author mostly wrote adult fantasy books and he recently published in the YA world. This is a book that I think is simply for everyone, I am always making a list of mental list of books I want to read to my kids and I am pretty sure this will be one of them.<br /><br />I honestly loved the writing because it was so easy to connect to everything in this book. The writing is very easy and that’s why I think it is a book for all. That does not mean it lacks memorable quotes because it had a fair share of those. The author can sometimes be spoon-feeding us the info but I did not care, I did not mind it because I was just so freaking happy while reading it.<br /><br /> <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Change often starts with the smallest of whispers. Like-minded people building it up to a roar.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />The characters are all memorable for me, I was initially planning to discuss all characters but I thought it is a better thing to discover them on the go. Ît has been more than 2 months since I finished the book and I still remember everything about it and that’s really rare for me unless I connect to the characters on a mythological level and I think Klune succeeded in doing that. There is the found family trope which was so well done, I loved how we were introduced to the characters slowly and then we get to know each of them on depth! Every single character was unique and I think that is challenging but the author simply nailed it. An additional thing I liked was that Linus the MC was 40 and he is unlike the too perfect male characters that are toxic and most YA books market for!<br /><br />The plot is not complicated and if I am being transparent her, it is very predictable but I think it is not about the plot at all. We have Linus who is a case-worker making sure that orphanages are fitting for the magical children and as the title implies he gets send to the house in the cerulean sea which is a top secret magic and the rest is history. But as I said above, the book is full of positive messages and it can be fluffy sometimes but I just needed that dose of serotonin very much and this book simply delivered!<br /><br /> <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“A home isn’t always the house we live in. It’s also the people we choose to surround ourselves with.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>Summary:</b> I consider this more a contemporary story with some magical settings so don’t expect something very fantasy driven. There is something magical about the story and I connected to everything very much that it left me crying in the hospital when I was reading the last pages! I simply love everything about this book and highly recommend it for all!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10432814259735545629" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Reading_ Tam_ Ishly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/102159719-reading-tam-ishly"><img alt="Reading_ Tam_ Ishly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578580640p2/102159719.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3276534324?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reading_ Tam_ Ishly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reading_ Tam_ Ishly" href="/user/show/102159719-reading-tam-ishly">Reading_ Tam_ Ishly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3276534324" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1151902297245525255">This is one goddamn fairytale. An original one. Which won't be retold in such perfection. I can see authors trying to tell their versions of this fairytale in 2050. Even then, they will find this hidden in the internet archives that once a reviewer gramma wrote this and they would be low-key panicking whenever there's the feeling of thinking of rewriting this precious goddamn fairytale 😎<br/><br/>There's this stepmother (mean, biased fairytale writers! Why only stepmothers are grouchy bad eh??!)...well, I</span>
  <span id="freeText1151902297245525255" style="display:none">This is one goddamn fairytale. An original one. Which won't be retold in such perfection. I can see authors trying to tell their versions of this fairytale in 2050. Even then, they will find this hidden in the internet archives that once a reviewer gramma wrote this and they would be low-key panicking whenever there's the feeling of thinking of rewriting this precious goddamn fairytale 😎<br /><br />There's this stepmother (mean, biased fairytale writers! Why only stepmothers are grouchy bad eh??!)...well, I repeat, there's this cruel, strict stepmother-like top organization which send formal check rounds to see if the orphanages were functioning prim and proper. <br /><br />A clueless prince is sent to an orphan home set miles away which an ocean (oh, Cerulean! Oh, it's a sea, not an ocean but the ocean is an ocean in the fairytale) seemingly keeps the living creatures (I meant that) in it separated from the rest of the world (sometimes I feel the word world is so undramatic. I wanted to use the universe or the galaxy. But that would not just fit.)<br /><br />So this prince arrives, gets entangled in a mess like situation which makes him feel like he's been made fun of, or not taken seriously at all, or just that he's been taken as someone easy to be with. <br /><br />And then there's this protective-as-heck-about-his-kids he. Yass, my he. The other he. (Stop it!) Nah. The he who's going to be the one who slow burns the grandma reviewer here with his being he. And these two hes will join forces in their fairy tale to actually fast burn the reader grandma towards the end with all their (beep..beep...beep). <br /><br />And then there's my (okay, they are my family now. So my. Mine.) I repeat, then there's my kids, oh the little naughty, cute, broken, scarred, beautiful, scary, wonderful, playful demons.<br /><br />(I didn't know I was the one who was going to write the retelling of this book. Nah. I would go and write the rest of this in my blog because GoodReads reviews are meant to have reviews...so here I go to my old blog. I have to write about the kids and the mayor and the two MCs!!!! 🙋 🎧 🧟 run don't walk away ⚔️ oh, she's sweet but a psycho 🎶<br /><br /> (Warning: this ain't a good review. Review? Forget it. It's just me going crazy about how much I love this book.)<br /><br /><br />Still in a daze. Since 5th September. The night I finished up reading this book and I am going to write a review which betrays justice. Yes, I am the criminal book reviewer reviewing books like my life depends on it when in real it's real. (See what I mean?!)<br /><br />***Book hangover. My damon babies 💕😭🤗🤛🤛 Arthur. Linus. Phee. Talia. Even Calliope.***<br /><br />*How can I ever get to get over this book?! 10 days after reading the book and I still feel the lump in my throat because I am still freaking happy and my feelings tend to crack like my heart cannot bear the love pain I have for the me-screaming-happy happy ending.<br /><br />Sorry, I don't think I will ever get to write a proper mean review about this book. Like ever. Because it always has its way to unravel the muscle fibres of my heart to distinct skeletal, smooth and cardiac. Yes, there's no going back!🙋</span>

<div id="review_3338661487" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3338661487" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3338661487?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3338661487" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6923295669617670598">OMG, this was so good! It really gave me All. The. Feels!<br/><br/>“The world is a weird and wonderful place. Why must we try and explain it all away? For our personal satisfaction?”<br/><br/>Linus Baker is a quiet man leading a quiet life. He’s a caseworker for the Department in Charge of Magical Youth, where he always follows the rules to a “t.” He doesn't question authority and does what's expected of him: nothing more, nothing less. Other than that, he lives with a cranky cat and his music to keep him company. </span>
  <span id="freeText6923295669617670598" style="display:none">OMG, this was so good! It really gave me All. The. Feels!<br /><br />“The world is a weird and wonderful place. Why must we try and explain it all away? For our personal satisfaction?”<br /><br />Linus Baker is a quiet man leading a quiet life. He’s a caseworker for the Department in Charge of Magical Youth, where he always follows the rules to a “t.” He doesn't question authority and does what's expected of him: nothing more, nothing less. Other than that, he lives with a cranky cat and his music to keep him company. It’s a lonely existence but he doesn’t know anything else.<br /><br />And then one day he is summoned by Extremely Upper Management and sent on a top secret assignment: to investigate the Marysas Orphanage, located on a remote island. The children that live there are supposedly unlike any Linus has ever seen—dangerously magical, apparently—and there’s a rumor one could bring about the End of Days. He is also urged to investigate the home's master, Arthur Parnassus, for reasons no one explains to him.<br /><br />When Linus arrives, he is shocked by what he finds, in that these children ARE different. Sure, they have the potential to be dangerous (particularly one), but they have the same needs of all children—to be loved and cared for, to be taken seriously, and to have their dreams nurtured. All of this definitely is happening thanks to the enigmatic Arthur Parnassus.<br /><br />What happens when a man who has always followed the rules and been led by his brain suddenly has his heart opened? What will that mean for his life, his job, and the children?<br /><br />One of the blurbs for <b>
  <i>The House in the Cerulean Sea</i>
</b> says it’s “very close to perfect,” and I couldn’t agree more. This is a gorgeous book about our tendency to fear what we don’t understand, the magic love can do, and the different meanings of family.<br /><br />This is a fantasy, of course, so it’s not for everyone, but while there are fantastical elements to the story, beyond that it's just a story about love and relationships and belonging. Boy, this is one I’ll remember and love for a long, long time.<br /><br />Check out my list of the best books I read in 2019 at <a href="https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2020/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2019.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2020/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2019.html</a>. <br /><br />Check out my list of the best books of the decade at <a href="https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2020/01/my-favorite-books-of-decade.html" target="”_blank”" rel="nofollow noopener">https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2020/01/my-favorite-books-of-decade.html</a>.<br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com</a>.<br /><br />Follow me on Instagram at <a href="https://www.instagram.com/the.bookishworld.of.yrralh/" target="”_blank”" rel="nofollow noopener"> https://www.instagram.com/the.bookishworld.of.yrralh/.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6923295669617670598" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3028501422" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3028501422" />
    <a title="Hollis " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16668577-hollis"><img alt="Hollis " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586714618p2/16668577.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3028501422?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hollis " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hollis " href="/user/show/16668577-hollis">Hollis </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781250217288" href="/book/show/45046567-the-house-in-the-cerulean-sea">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=family-focused">family-focused</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=all-the-lols">all-the-lols</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=all-the-feels">all-the-feels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=finished-in-january-2020">finished-in-january-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3028501422" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6224094750641844258"><b> June 22, 2020 : huge price drop/sale alert!! for the <a href='https://www.amazon.ca/House-Cerulean-Sea-TJ-Klune-ebook/dp/B07QPHT8CB/ref=sr_1_1?crid=37LR74QLEMR62&dchild=1&keywords=house+on+the+cerulean+sea&qid=1592853348&sprefix=house+on+the%2Caps%2C169&sr=8-1' rel='nofollow noopener'> Canucks</a>. for the <a href='https://www.amazon.com/House-Cerulean-Sea-TJ-Klune-ebook/dp/B07QPHT8CB/ref=sr_1_1?crid=2CJZMFXE79HSD&dchild=1&keywords=house+on+the+cerulean+sea&qid=1592853335&sprefix=house+on+the%2Caps%2C165&sr=8-1' rel='nofollow noopener'>'Muricans</a>. only until June 28, 2020.</b><br/><br/>----<br/><br/>This book was a delightfully sweet and lovely cup of heartbreak, melancholy, and wonder. Which sounds almost awful, or hella sad, and probably contradicts the vibe the cover is putting out, but I don't know how else to describe all the things this made me feel.<br/><br/>There is whimsy and wonder in this world where magical people exists, there's melancholy in the reality that children who demon</span>
  <span id="freeText6224094750641844258" style="display:none"><b> June 22, 2020 : huge price drop/sale alert!! for the <a href="https://www.amazon.ca/House-Cerulean-Sea-TJ-Klune-ebook/dp/B07QPHT8CB/ref=sr_1_1?crid=37LR74QLEMR62&amp;dchild=1&amp;keywords=house+on+the+cerulean+sea&amp;qid=1592853348&amp;sprefix=house+on+the%2Caps%2C169&amp;sr=8-1" rel="nofollow noopener"> Canucks</a>. for the <a href="https://www.amazon.com/House-Cerulean-Sea-TJ-Klune-ebook/dp/B07QPHT8CB/ref=sr_1_1?crid=2CJZMFXE79HSD&amp;dchild=1&amp;keywords=house+on+the+cerulean+sea&amp;qid=1592853335&amp;sprefix=house+on+the%2Caps%2C165&amp;sr=8-1" rel="nofollow noopener">'Muricans</a>. only until June 28, 2020.</b><br /><br />----<br /><br />This book was a delightfully sweet and lovely cup of heartbreak, melancholy, and wonder. Which sounds almost awful, or hella sad, and probably contradicts the vibe the cover is putting out, but I don't know how else to describe all the things this made me feel.<br /><br />There is whimsy and wonder in this world where magical people exists, there's melancholy in the reality that children who demonstrate these abilities are sequestered in orphanages and regulated schools or programs, monitored by the government with caseworkers who ensure their safety and well-being, and there's sweetness in the particular caseworker we follow, Linus; a round middle-aged man believed to be wholly unremarkable, friendless but for his cat, who is in fact so much of the opposite. <br /><br />"<i>I'm afraid I don't have magic.</i>"<br />"<b>You do, Mr. Baker. Arthur told me that there can be magic in the ordinary.</b>"<br /><br />There were so many moments that had me a hair's breadth away from crying. I welled up, swallowing hard, like.. six times? Probably more. At one point I was almost wrecked by a bloody button. And then, of course, there was a moment near the end where I just let go. Had my cry. I own it. The emotion Klune packs into his writing resonates so strongly and hits even harder because of the children in this story. Sal, in particular, just.. wow, yeah, I have no words. <br /><br />Like Linus, it is impossible to remain impartial in the face of these children who were unwanted, unloved, or deemed too dangerous, too unique, to be anywhere else but this little island, far away from others. Through the narrative, Klune challenges prejudice, racism, and mob mentality, and does it beautifully. This is the perfect story for our time, our current climate, and it's delightfully unique because of the circumstances and the rare collection of gems that are these atypical characters. Truly, the creativity of this story is something else.<br /><br />I loved this book so much. For all the heavier topics and bittersweetness of it all, this was a lot of fun, too. It's silly, weird, and delightfully charming, full of emotion and hope and love. <br /><br />I definitely recommend. Particularly right now.<br /><br /><br />** I received an ARC from Edelweiss and the publisher (thank you!) in exchange for an honest review. **<br /><br />---<br /><br />This review can also be found at <a href="https://atakefromtwocities.home.blog/2020/03/16/the-house-in-the-cerulean-sea-by-tj-klune/" rel="nofollow noopener">A Take From Two Cities</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6224094750641844258" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3480478139" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3480478139" />
    <a title="Fadwa (Word Wonders)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42662881-fadwa-word-wonders"><img alt="Fadwa (Word Wonders)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590785619p2/42662881.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3480478139?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fadwa (Word Wonders)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fadwa (Word Wonders)" href="/user/show/42662881-fadwa-word-wonders">Fadwa (Word Wonders)</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42662881-fadwa-word-wonders?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42662881-fadwa-word-wonders?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42662881-fadwa-word-wonders?shelf=2020-releases">2020-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42662881-fadwa-word-wonders?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42662881-fadwa-word-wonders?shelf=lgbtq-m-m">lgbtq-m-m</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3480478139" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12233084143330731543"><b>CW: trauma, fatphobia both internalized and otherwise (challenged), dieting, bigotry, discussion of child abuse</b><br/><br/>THIS BOOK MADE ME SO HAPPYYYYYYYYYY!!! It's the embodiment of sunshine, if happiness could be a single book it would be this one and here is why:<br/><br/>- <b>Found family excellence</b>: genuinely one of the best found families I've ever read about. So eclectic and all over the place but so loving and supportive. The way Arthur loves the children, the way they have each other's backs, the way Zoe is e</span>
  <span id="freeText12233084143330731543" style="display:none"><b>CW: trauma, fatphobia both internalized and otherwise (challenged), dieting, bigotry, discussion of child abuse</b><br /><br />THIS BOOK MADE ME SO HAPPYYYYYYYYYY!!! It's the embodiment of sunshine, if happiness could be a single book it would be this one and here is why:<br /><br />- <b>Found family excellence</b>: genuinely one of the best found families I've ever read about. So eclectic and all over the place but so loving and supportive. The way Arthur loves the children, the way they have each other's backs, the way Zoe is everyone's mama bear and Linus comes fits right in. Ugh. So good.<br /><br />- <b>THE MAGICAL CHILDREN</b>: okay, i know children in books can be a huge turn off for many people but you're going to find yourself endeared and wanting to protect this group of kids without even realizing it. Especially since they're all traumatized and finding solace in their home and each other, learning to trust happiness and healing. It all made me so emotional. Lucy, the antichrist, who can deadpan the most morbid of one liners but wouldn't hurt a fly and loves adventures and cooking. Sal, the boy who hurts a lot and talks very little. Talia the gnome. Theodore, and a few more. They're all so wonderful.<br /><br />- <b>The trauma depiction and exploration</b>: I mentioned it above but, each one of these kids as well as Arthur have a hard a hard childhood, every single one. And if shows differently in every one of them so I loved seeing the different manifestations of trauma in different people and how that showed that on one experience is universal. Not only that, but it also showed healing and how every person heal sat their own pace and in their own way. There is no one correct way to do it.<br /><br />- <b>Linus' character arc</b> One of the best character developments I've read about. The way he goes from being a rule following pushover no matter how unfair those rules are, to learning that sometimes rules are used as an oppression tool to finally fighting the oppressive institution. <i>chef's kiss.</i>). Especially since eventhough he opened himself up, got out of his comfort zone and started speaking up, his essence stayed the same. That of a genuinely good awkward guide who just needed a nudge in the right direction to do the right thing. <br /><br />- <b>Slowest of burns m/m romance</b> LINUS AND ARTHUR!!!!!!!!!!! So cute! So pure! It's so so slow and you can just feel their feelings falling into place as you read without it being spelled out for you. And I loved (and found kind of funny) the fact that even while familiarizing themselves with each other and falling with each other, they kept being all posh and proper in their interactions.<br /><br />JUST PICK UP THIS BOOK FOR AN INSTANTANEOUS SHOT OF SEROTONIN!!!!!!!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12233084143330731543" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3236962158" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3236962158" />
    <a title="amy ☂︎" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/61624004-amy"><img alt="amy ☂︎" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595924086p2/61624004.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3236962158?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="amy ☂︎" class="user" itemprop="url" name="amy ☂︎" href="/user/show/61624004-amy">amy ☂︎</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61624004-amy?shelf=favs">favs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61624004-amy?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61624004-amy?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61624004-amy?shelf=lgbtq-rep">lgbtq-rep</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3236962158" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15036414880346183924">I've sat down to write this review more times than I can count. I'm still torn between wanting <i>The House in the Cerulean Sea</i> all to myself and wanting to scream <b>I LOVE THIS BOOK FURIOUSLY</b> at the top of my lungs. <br/><br/>Have you ever loved something on such a deeply personal level that it feels almost impossible to convey that exact feeling to someone else? That whatever you say is pointless anyway, because the person on the other side <i>isn't you</i> and they will never be able to fully comprehend what touch</span>
  <span id="freeText15036414880346183924" style="display:none">I've sat down to write this review more times than I can count. I'm still torn between wanting <i>The House in the Cerulean Sea</i> all to myself and wanting to scream <b>I LOVE THIS BOOK FURIOUSLY</b> at the top of my lungs. <br /><br />Have you ever loved something on such a deeply personal level that it feels almost impossible to convey that exact feeling to someone else? That whatever you say is pointless anyway, because the person on the other side <i>isn't you</i> and they will never be able to fully comprehend what touches your soul in what exact way?<br /><br />To be blatantly honest with you: <b>I don't know if you will like this book as much as I did.</b> Honestly? Maybe you won't. Maybe, to you, it's just a story that won't have a big impact on your life whatsoever. Maybe you won't connect to any of the characters. Maybe you'll forget about this world the day after you've left it. <br />But maybe,<i> just maybe</i>, it will touch you in a similar way that it touched me. Maybe it will brighten your life a little. Maybe the characters will stay with you a little longer.<br /><br /><b>This gentle thing healed my entire fragile soul and gave me a sense of peace and happiness that I had been lacking for a long time.</b> This book, to me, felt like a long-needed hug after a time of emptiness and loneliness. Or like a good friend taking you by the hand and telling you, "You got this! And I'm right here with you."<br /><br />And that's all I have to say. That's all I <i>can</i> say.<br /><br />Thank you, <i>The House in the Cerulean Sea</i>.</span>

<div id="review_3553828893" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3553828893" />
    <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik"><img alt="Nilufer Ozmekik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559807601p2/53701594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3553828893?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nilufer Ozmekik" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik">Nilufer Ozmekik</a>
